--- Research Result 1 ---
Okay, I will conduct targeted Google Searches to gather the most recent, credible information on "anomaly detection long-term surveillance video datasets labeled 2024-2025" and synthesize it into a verifiable text artifact.
Based on the search results, here's a summary of recent developments in anomaly detection for long-term surveillance video datasets, focusing on datasets labeled in 2024-2025:

**General Trends and Challenges:**

*   **Importance:** Anomaly detection in surveillance videos is crucial for public safety, traffic management, and security, with applications in crime detection, accident analysis, and intelligent monitoring.
*   **Challenges:** Detecting anomalies in long-term surveillance video is challenging due to the context-dependent nature of anomalies (time of day, day of week, etc.), variations in lighting and weather, and the difficulty of tracking individuals in crowded scenes. Existing methods often struggle with causal inference and anomaly understanding in real-world surveillance contexts. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0)
*   **Need for Better Datasets:** There's a recognized need for comprehensive datasets with diverse scenarios to train superior models. Existing datasets may lack diversity, contain semantic ambiguity in anomaly categories, or focus on single scenes. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1)

**Datasets and Benchmarks:**

*   **MSAD (Multi-Scenario Anomaly Detection):** Introduced in late 2024, this dataset comprises 14 distinct scenarios from various camera views, featuring diverse motion patterns and challenging variations in lighting and weather. [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [mdpi](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3) It aims to provide a robust foundation for training better models. [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2)
*   **PreVAD (Pre-training Video Anomaly Dataset):** As of March 2025, this is described as the largest and most diverse video anomaly dataset to date, featuring 35,279 annotated videos with multi-level category labels and descriptions that explicitly define anomalies. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1)
*   **SurveillanceVQA-589K:** Introduced in May 2025, this is a large-scale question answering (QA) benchmark tailored for the surveillance domain. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) It contains approximately 589,000 question-answer pairs, including 12 QA types covering both normal and abnormal video content. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0)
*   **UCVL:** Introduced in February 2025, this benchmark is designed for multi-task anomaly analysis in crime surveillance video. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) It integrates crime labels from UCF-Crime and segment-level human descriptions from UCF-Crime Annotation datasets. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4)
*   **VANE-Bench:** Introduced in April 2025, this benchmark evaluates Video Anomaly Detection (VAD) in both real-world and AI-generated videos, providing a targeted benchmark for this task. [aclanthology](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) The VANE-Bench dataset encompasses a variety of categories derived from both real-world surveillance footage and AI-generated video clips. [aclanthology](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5)
*   **CamNuvem:** A dataset focused on robbery videos, containing 486 real-world robbery surveillance videos acquired from public sources. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6)
*   **UCF-Crime:** A widely used dataset consisting of 1900 long and untrimmed real-world surveillance videos with 13 realistic anomalies. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7)

**Approaches and Methods:**

*   **Context-Aware Anomaly Detection:** Algorithms like Trinity are being developed to consider the context (time of day, day of week, schedule of events) when detecting anomalies in long-term surveillance.
*   **Meta-Learning:** Meta-learning frameworks are being used for faster adaptation of anomaly detection models to new camera viewpoints or environmental variations.
*   **Language-Guided Open-World VAD:** Methods like LaGoVAD are emerging to address the challenge of variable anomaly definitions, allowing guided detection through user-provided natural language. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1)
*   **Use of Large Language Models (LLMs):** LLMs are being harnessed for training-free video anomaly detection, video anomaly detection and explanation, and for generating question-answer pairs for video anomaly analysis.

**Key Papers and Resources:**

*   **"Advancing Video Anomaly Detection: A Concise Review and a New Dataset" (Zhu et al., 2024):** Introduces the MSAD dataset and provides a review of video anomaly detection. [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2)
*   **"Context-aware Video Anomaly Detection in Long-Term Datasets" (Yang & Radke, 2024):** Proposes the Trinity algorithm for context-aware anomaly detection.
*   **"SurveillanceVQA-589K: A Benchmark for Comprehensive Surveillance Video-Language Understanding with Large Models" (2025):** Introduces the SurveillanceVQA-589K dataset for video question answering. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0)
*   **"Rethinking Metrics and Benchmarks of Video Anomaly Detection" (2025):** Discusses biases in existing metrics and benchmarks and proposes new metrics and benchmarks.
*   **"VANE-Bench: Video Anomaly Evaluation Benchmark for Conversational LMMs" (2025):** Introduces the VANE-Bench dataset for evaluating LMMs in video anomaly detection. [aclanthology](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5)
*   **"Awesome Video Anomaly Detection" GitHub repository:** A curated list of resources for video anomaly detection.

This information should provide a solid overview of the current state of research and datasets related to anomaly detection in long-term surveillance videos, with a focus on resources labeled or published in 2024-2025.

Based on the search results, here's a summary of information related to anomaly detection in long-term video surveillance, focusing on GitHub repositories, models, and weights, with an emphasis on developments in 2024-2025:

**General Trends and Concepts:**

*   **AI-Powered Surveillance:** AI is revolutionizing surveillance and anomaly detection by enabling real-time monitoring, automated threat detection, and efficient responses. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) These systems use machine learning, computer vision, and big data for accurate and proactive security. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) (Source: 4)
*   **Anomaly Detection Techniques:** Common techniques include machine learning (supervised, unsupervised, deep learning), statistical models (threshold-based), hybrid approaches (rule-based and AI integration), and behavioral analysis. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) Deep learning techniques like autoencoders are also used. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) (Source: 4)
*   **Real-time Video Analytics:** AI-powered surveillance is achieving advanced video analysis, detecting complex behaviors and interactions in high-density environments. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) Multi-modal AI systems combine visual, audio, and spatial data for holistic surveillance. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) Future systems will incorporate predictive analytics to forecast potential anomalies based on historical trends and real-time data. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) (Source: 4)
*   **Emphasis on Ethical AI:** There's increasing emphasis on ethical AI to prevent misuse, bias, and over-surveillance, prioritizing transparent and accountable AI systems. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) (Source: 4)
*   **Standardization:** A push towards standardized, interoperable AI models for surveillance systems is emerging to ensure seamless communication and scalability. Open-source AI frameworks are becoming more popular. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) (Source: 4)
*   **Anomaly detection focus:** Anomaly detection is focused on identifying patterns that don't match expected behaviors, flagging defects, errors, or irregular activities that could otherwise go unnoticed. [ultralytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) (Source: 14)

**GitHub Repositories and Models:**

*   **Awesome Anomaly Detection with Large Language Models (LLMs):** A GitHub repository provides a curated list of papers and code related to anomaly detection using LLMs for various data types (tabular, time series, image, video, graph, text, log). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2) (Source: 1)
*   **Holmes-VAU:** A GitHub repository provides the official implementation of "Holmes-VAU: Towards Long-term Video Anomaly Understanding at Any Granularity" (CVPR 2025 Highlight). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3) It introduces HIVAU-70k, a large-scale benchmark for hierarchical video anomaly understanding. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3) It also proposes an Anomaly-focused Temporal Sampler (ATS) for efficient anomaly detection in long videos. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3) (Source: 3)
*   **LAVAD (LAnguage-based VAD):** A method tackling VAD in a novel, training-free paradigm, exploiting the capabilities of pre-trained large language models (LLMs) and existing vision-language models (VLMs). [youtube](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4) (Source: 8)
*   **Track Any Anomalous Object (TAO):** A novel VAD framework that integrates the detection of multiple fine-grained anomalous objects into a unified framework. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-5) (Source: 9) [opensearch](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-6)
*   **OpenSearch Project:** The OpenSearch project roadmap for 2024-2025 includes enhancements to anomaly detection capabilities within its observability and security analytics themes. (Source: 17) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7)
*   **Video Anomaly Detection List:** There is a GitHub list called "Awesome Video Anomaly Detection". [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-8) (Source: 5) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-9)

**Specific Models and Approaches:**

*   **LLMs for Video Anomaly Detection:** Several papers explore the use of Large Language Models (LLMs) for video anomaly detection. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-10) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7) Some approaches involve using VLMs to generate textual descriptions of video frames and then using LLMs to estimate anomaly scores. [youtube](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-10) (Sources: 1, 6, 8)
*   **EventVAD:** A training-free video anomaly detection framework that dynamically generates multimodal text descriptions and analyzes them for efficient anomaly detection by fusing visual language models, audio language models and large language models. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7) (Source: 13)
*   **VADSK:** A lightweight pipeline for anomaly classification using keyword weights, leveraging foundational models' feature representation generalization capabilities. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-10) (Source: 6) [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0)
*   **Deep BiLSTM Attention Model:** An attention-based anomaly detection system analyzes spatiotemporal features and focuses on long-term patterns. (Source: 10)
*   **YOLO11:** Vision AI systems like Ultralytics YOLO11 can analyze details in images like shape, texture, and structure, making it easier to spot irregularities quickly and accurately. (Source: 14)

**Datasets and Benchmarks:**

*   **HIVAU-70k:** A large-scale benchmark for hierarchical video anomaly understanding across any granularity. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3) (Source: 3)
*   **SurveillanceVQA-589K:** A large-scale QA dataset specifically designed for surveillance videos. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-11) The dataset consists of four surveillance video datasets as video sources and contains approximately 589,000 question-answer pairs, including 12 QA types covering both normal and abnormal video content, such as factual summarization, behavior/spatial-temporal analysis, causal reasoning, anomaly detection, etc. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-11) (Source: 2)
*   **MSAD (Multi-Scenario Anomaly Detection):** A new dataset comprising 14 distinct scenarios captured from various camera views. [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-12) (Source: 7)

**Key Research Directions:**

*   **Training-Free Methods:** A significant trend is the development of training-free video anomaly detection methods that leverage pre-trained models (VLMs and LLMs). [youtube](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4) (Sources: 8, 13)
*   **Granular Analysis:** Research is moving towards finer-grained analysis, such as detecting anomalous pixels, to capture a broader range of anomalies. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-5) (Source: 9) [opensearch](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-6)
*   **Multi-Modal Approaches:** Combining visual, audio, and textual information is becoming more common for improved anomaly detection. (Source: 4)
*   **Open-Vocabulary Anomaly Detection:** Leveraging pre-trained large models to detect and categorize seen and unseen anomalies. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-13) (Source: 16)
*   **Temporal Anomaly Detection:** Focuses on detecting changes over time, such as deviations in activity patterns. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) (Source: 4)


--- Research Result 3 ---
Okay, I will conduct targeted Google Searches to gather the most recent, credible information on "long-term surveillance video dataset same scene anomaly detection" and synthesize it into a verifiable text artifact.
Based on the search results, here's a synthesis of information on long-term surveillance video dataset same scene anomaly detection:

**1. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) The Challenge of Long-Term Surveillance Anomaly Detection:**

*   Real-world surveillance cameras operate for extended periods (months or years), making the context crucial for anomaly detection. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) The definition of "normal" changes based on factors like time of day, day of week, and schedules. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2) [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-3) Algorithms need to account for these time-varying patterns.
*   Traditional anomaly detection research often focuses on short, isolated video clips, lacking contextual awareness. [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) This limits their applicability to real-world camera networks. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1)
*   Manual anomaly detection in long video sequences is time-consuming and requires significant effort due to the low probability of abnormal events. [diva-portal](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-4) This also makes creating annotated datasets difficult. [diva-portal](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-4)
*   Environmental factors (background noise, occlusions, illumination changes, atmospheric turbulence) pose difficulties for accurate anomaly detection.
*   Anomalous events are uncommon and their behavior is typically sparse, making it difficult to use a single technique to identify every kind of anomaly. [ekb](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-5) [diva-portal](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-4)

**2. Datasets:**

*   **Limitations of Existing Datasets:** Many popular datasets simulate anomalies using humans but don't consider diverse and complex environmental conditions, making it difficult for models to detect real-world anomalies. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) Many datasets are short and isolated.
*   **Need for Better Datasets:** There's a need for publicly available benchmarked datasets for anomaly identification due to the uneven distribution of normal and abnormal data. [ekb](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-5)
*   **WF Dataset:** A public webcam-based dataset spanning over three months of activity was created to address the video-context correspondence problem. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) It contains videos of the same location under various lighting, weather, and crowding conditions. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1)
*   **MSAD Dataset:** A new dataset, Multi-Scenario Anomaly Detection (MSAD), comprising 14 distinct scenarios captured from various camera views, has diverse motion patterns and challenging variations, such as different lighting and weather conditions. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6) It contains 35 human-related anomalies (HRA) and 20 non-human-related anomalies (NHRA). [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6)
*   **UMAD Benchmark Dataset:** The UMAD Benchmark Dataset is designed specifically for anomaly detection with reference in robotic patrolling scenarios. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-7)
*   **UCVL:** A MLLM benchmark designed for multi-task anomaly analysis in crime surveillance video. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) It leverages the previous anomaly datasets by integrating the crime labels from UCF-Crime (UCC) and the segment-level human descriptions from UCF-Crime Annotation (UCA). [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0)
*   **Real-World Dataset:** A large-scale video anomaly detection dataset consisting of 1900 real-world surveillance videos of 13 different anomalous events and normal activities captured by surveillance cameras. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-8)

**3. Approaches and Methods:**

*   **Context-Aware Anomaly Detection:** Algorithms like Trinity are designed to be context-aware, learning alignments between context, appearance, and motion to classify videos. [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1)
*   **Deep Learning Methods:** Deep learning has shown great promise in solving crowd anomaly detection. [ijisae](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-9) Deep learning anomaly detection technologies overruled the traditional machine learning systems. [ijisae](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-9)
*   **CNN and LSTM:** CNN and CNN-LSTM based approaches are used for detection and classification of abnormal events. [uab](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10) The CNN architecture is developed from scratch and can be used for spatial domains. [uab](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10) LSTM architecture is developed for the temporal domain. [uab](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-10)
*   **Hybrid YOLOv8 + CNN:** A robust hybrid model that integrates YOLOv8 and Convolutional Neural Networks (CNN) for real-time accident detection and vehicle number plate recognition. [scitepress](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-11)
*   **Bi-LSTM:** An innovative attention-based anomaly detection system designed to analyze spatiotemporal features and focus on long-term patterns to identify anomalies in video frames. [mdpi](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-12) This system integrates a CNN equipped with attention modules to improve feature learning, alongside a Bi-LSTM network that leverages attention weights to emphasize crucial details for motion detection. [mdpi](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-12)
*   **Few-Shot Learning:** Few-shot learning aims to adapt quickly to a new task with only a few training samples. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6)

**4. Challenges and Future Directions:**

*   **Real-time decision making:** Real-time decision making is an important but mostly neglected factor. [usf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-13)
*   **Few-shot learning, continual learning, cross-domain adaptability:** These are important for adapting to new information in a scene over time or adapting to a different scene. [usf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-13)
*   **Explainability:** There is a need for explainable anomaly detection.
*   **Integration with Existing Systems:** AI surveillance system needs to seamlessly connect with current video management software (VMS) and security infrastructure through standardized APIs and protocols. [forasoft](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-14)
*   **Ethical Considerations:** Ethical considerations need to be addressed.
*   **Future Trends:** Potential future trends in anomaly detection, including the development of more sophisticated datasets, exploration of hybrid architectural models, integration of multi-camera systems, advancement in open-set action recognition algorithms, model development for cutting-edge process automation systems, harnessing the potential of IoT, leveraging edge computing, and incorporating drone technologies into anomaly detection strategies. [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-15)

**5. [ekb](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-5) Applications:**

*   Traffic accident detection, criminal activity detection, and illegal activity detection. [mdpi](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-16)
*   Security surveillance, traffic monitoring, industrial monitoring, and healthcare. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-6)
*   Retail security to industrial safety monitoring. [forasoft](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-14)
*   Museum security. [forasoft](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-14)
*   Robotic patrolling. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-7)

*   **Dataset:** The HIVAU-70k dataset is available (Source: \[1]). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) This is a large-scale benchmark for hierarchical video anomaly understanding (Source: \[1, 3, 4, 5, 6]). It contains over 70,000 multi-granular annotations organized at clip-level, event-level, and video-level segments (Source: \[1, 3, 5, 6]). [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0)

The Holmes-VAU repository is the official implementation of the paper "Holmes-VAU: Towards Long-term Video Anomaly Understanding at Any Granularity" (Source: \[1]). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) The model utilizes an Anomaly-focused Temporal Sampler (ATS) to efficiently detect anomalies in long videos (Source: \[1, 3, 5, 6]). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) The ATS integrates an anomaly scorer with a density-aware sampler to focus on anomaly-rich regions (Source: \[1, 3, 6]). [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1)

--- Research Result 5 ---
Based on the search results, here's how you can access the MSAD dataset for anomaly detection in long-term surveillance videos:

**Two distinct MSAD datasets exist:**

1.  **MSAD (Model Selection for Anomaly Detection in Time Series):**

    *   This dataset is related to model selection for anomaly detection in time series data. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
    *   **Download:** The dataset can be downloaded from the GitHub repository "[boniolp/MSAD](https://github.com/boniolp/MSAD)". [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
    *   **Installation:**
        *   Clone the repository using Git: `git clone https://github.com/boniolp/MSAD.git` [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
        *   Navigate to the directory: `cd MSAD/`
        *   Download the datasets and weights from the provided links in the repository (due to GitHub size limitations, they are hosted on Google Drive). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
        *   Move the downloaded `TSB.zip` file into the `MSAD/data/` directory and unzip it. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
        *   Unzip the `data.zip` file and move its contents into the `MSAD/data/` directory to skip generating Oracles and creating processed datasets. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
        *   Unzip the `weights.zip` file and move its contents (supervised/ and unsupervised/) into the `MSAD/results/weights/` directory. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
        *   Create and activate a conda environment named MSAD. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
    *   **Description:** The dataset includes labeled real-world and artificial time series data, such as AWS server metrics, online advertisement clicking rates, real-time traffic data, and Twitter mentions of large publicly-traded companies. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) It also includes the SensorScope dataset (environmental data) and the YAHOO dataset (real and synthetic time series based on Yahoo production traffic). [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)

2.  **MSAD (Multi-Scenario Anomaly Detection):**

    *   This is a newer dataset specifically designed for video anomaly detection. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3)
    *   **Availability:** The MSAD dataset is available for download, but access to the original video format requires filling out an application form. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)
    *   **Project Website:** Refer to the project website for more details and the application form. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)
    *   **Feature Download:** Extracted features (I3D and Video-Swin Transformer) are also available for download. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2)
    *   **GitHub Repository:** Code for benchmarking the MSAD dataset is available at "[NeurIPS 2024] MSAD - A Benchmark for Video Anomaly Detection - GitHub". [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)
    *   **License:** The dataset is strictly for academic and research purposes. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) Commercial use, reproduction, distribution, or sale of the dataset or derivative works are prohibited. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)
    *   **Protocols:** The dataset supports two evaluation protocols: [neurips](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5)
        *   **(i) Self-Supervised Methods:** Train on 360 normal videos from 14 scenarios and test on the remaining 120 normal videos and 240 abnormal videos. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)
        *   **(ii) Weakly-Supervised Methods:** Train on 360 normal and 120 abnormal videos (video-level annotations only), and test on 120 normal and 120 abnormal videos. This GitHub repo only supports Protocol ii. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)
    *   **Description:** This dataset comprises 14 distinct scenarios captured from various camera views, featuring diverse motion patterns and challenging variations in lighting and weather conditions. [neurips](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) [neurips](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5) [openreview](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [researchgate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8) [mdpi](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) It includes 35 human-related and 20 non-human-related anomaly types. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [neurips](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) The videos are sourced from platforms like YouTube, Itemfix, and Bilibili. [neurips](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)

It is important to note the publication dates of the resources. The "Advancing Video Anomaly Detection: A Concise Review and a New Dataset" paper related to the Multi-Scenario Anomaly Detection (MSAD) dataset was accepted to NeurIPS 2024. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5)

Based on the search results, here's a summary of the licensing terms for the HIVAU-70k dataset and the code associated with the Holmes-VAU repository:

**1. Holmes-VAU Repository Code:**

*   The code associated with the Holmes-VAU repository is released under the **MIT License**.[1, 10]

**2. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-0) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-1) HIVAU-70k Dataset:**

*   The HIVAU-70k dataset is available for research purposes [1, 7, 15].
*   The dataset is a large-scale benchmark for hierarchical video anomaly understanding [1, 7, 15]. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-2) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-3) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-1) It contains over 70,000 multi-granular annotations organized at clip-level, event-level, and video-level segments [1, 7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-3) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-1) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-2)
*   The HIVAU-70k benchmark is available now [19]. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-2) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-3) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-4)
*   The dataset is built upon the UCF-Crime and XD-Violence datasets [7]. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-1)
*   When using the HIVAU-70k dataset, it's important to adhere to the terms of CC BY-NC-SA 4.0 and licenses of other source datasets [16]. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-0)

**General Considerations for AI/ML Data Licensing:**

*   **Data-Centric Licenses:** Licensing datasets is a significant aspect of AI development. [viso](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-6) [galkinlaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-7) The license is a legal agreement controlling the modification, distribution, and use of datasets [2]. [viso](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-6)
*   **Scope of Use:**  Clarify whether the data can be used for commercial purposes, research, or both [3].
*   **Attribution:** Check if the data provider requires attribution and how it should be given [3]. [galkinlaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-7) [cancerimagingarchive](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-8)
*   **Compliance:** Ensure your use complies with GDPR, CCPA, or other applicable data protection laws [3, 4]. [futurebeeai](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-9) [galkinlaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-7)
*   **Restrictions:** Be aware of restrictions on data transfer across geographic boundaries, which might affect how data can be stored and accessed [3]. [galkinlaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-7) Datasets cannot be resold, shared, sublicensed, or publicly distributed, including on open-source platforms [4]. [futurebeeai](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-9)
*   **Ethical Use:** Datasets should not be used for biased, unethical, or harmful AI applications, such as discriminatory AI models or illegal surveillance [4]. [futurebeeai](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/5-9)

It's important to consult the specific license files within the Holmes-VAU repository and any accompanying documentation for the HIVAU-70k dataset to ensure full compliance with the terms and conditions.


--- Research Result 7 ---
Based on the search results, here's a summary of information regarding EventVAD and VADSK for anomaly detection tasks:

**EventVAD:**

*   **Description:** EventVAD is a training-free video anomaly detection framework that combines dynamic graph architectures and multimodal Large Language Models (LLMs) through temporal-event reasoning. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-2) It addresses the limitations of existing training-free methods in localizing fine-grained visual transitions and diverse events within videos. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-2)
*   **Methodology:**
    1.  **Event-Aware Dynamic Graph Construction:** Employs dynamic spatiotemporal graph modeling with time-decay constraints to capture event-aware video features. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3)
    2.  **Graph Attention Networks (GAN) Propagation:** Refines frame representations while preserving temporal consistency using a training-free attention mechanism based on orthogonal feature projection. [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3)
    3.  **Statistical Boundary Detection:** Performs adaptive noise filtering and uses signal ratio thresholding to detect event boundaries via unsupervised statistical features. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) This reduces the complexity of processing long videos for MLLMs and improves their temporal reasoning through event consistency. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0)
    4.  **Event-Centric Anomaly Scoring:** Utilizes a hierarchical prompting strategy to guide MLLMs in performing reasoning before determining final decisions.
*   **Performance:** Achieves state-of-the-art (SOTA) results in training-free settings on the UCF-Crime and XD-Violence datasets, outperforming strong baselines that use 7B or larger MLLMs. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3)
*   **Code:** No code implementations were found in the search results.
*   **Pre-trained Models/Weights:** EventVAD uses the ViT-B/16 of EVA-CLIP (Sun et al., 2023) and enhances inter-frame features using RAFT optical flow (Teed and Deng, 2020). It inputs the segmented events into an MLLM (Cheng et al., 2024) for scoring. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-2)
*   **Usage Examples:** Evaluated on the UCF-Crime and XD-Violence datasets.

**VADSK:**

*   **Description:** VADSK is a lightweight pipeline for anomaly classification using keyword weights. It employs a two-stage process: induction followed by deduction. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)
*   **Methodology:**
    1.  **Induction:** Descriptions are generated from normal and anomalous frames to identify and assign weights to relevant keywords. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) Randomly sampled normal and anomalous frames are passed through a pre-trained foundational model to output corresponding descriptions of those frames. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-6) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) Next, the normal and anomalous descriptions are passed through a TF-IDF operation, outputting a corresponding TF-IDF matrix of scores. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)
    2.  **Deduction:** Inference frame descriptions are converted into keyword encodings using induction-derived weights for input into a neural network for anomaly classification. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)
*   **Performance:** Achieved comparable performance on the three benchmarks UCSD Ped2, Shanghai Tech, and CUHK Avenue, with ROC AUC scores of 0.865, 0.745, and 0.742, respectively. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4)
*   **Code:** No direct link to a GitHub repository was found in the search results.
*   **Pre-trained Models/Weights:** Uses a pre-trained foundational model to generate captions that differentiate anomaly cases from normal scene behavior. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)
*   **Usage Examples:** Evaluated on the UCSD Ped2, Shanghai Tech, and CUHK Avenue datasets. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4)

It's important to note that both EventVAD and VADSK leverage pre-trained models and/or LLMs to achieve anomaly detection without extensive training data.


--- Research Result 8 ---
Based on the search results, here's a summary of anomaly labeling in datasets and the conditions of use:

**Anomaly Labeling in Datasets:**

*   **Types of Anomalies:** Datasets can include various types of anomalies, such as:
    *   Abnormal events in video sequences, including crashes, fires, and violence [7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-0)
    *   Anomalous activities detected via webcams [9]. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-1)
    *   Deviations from the norm in manufacturing, medical imaging, agriculture, retail, and other scenarios [13]. [landing](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-2)
    *   Contextual anomalies, where events are normal but occur in an unexpected context (e.g., people entering a campus on a weekend) [9].
    *   Pseudo-contextual anomalies, where existing videos are given an incorrect context label [9]. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-1)
*   **Labeling Methods:**
    *   **Video-level labels:** Indicate whether a video is abnormal or normal and the type of anomaly [7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-0)
    *   **Frame-level labels:** Identify abnormal or normal video frames [7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-0)
    *   **Bounding box annotations:** Mark the location of anomalous events within a frame [9].
    *   **Normal/Abnormal classes:** Datasets may have built-in classes for "Normal" and "Abnormal" cases [13]. [landing](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-2)
*   **Unlabeled Data:** Some anomaly detection methods work with unlabeled or partially labeled data, identifying patterns without predefined classes [11]. [datarobot](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-3)

**Conditions of Use for Datasets:**

*   **Creative Commons Licenses:** Many datasets are released under Creative Commons licenses, such as CC BY 4.0 or CC BY 3.0, which allow users to share and adapt the data with attribution [2, 4, 18].
*   **Attribution Requirements:** Some datasets require attribution to the original sources, especially when they incorporate data from other open data projects [3]. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-4) Crediting the dataset creators and linking back to the license is often recommended [3].
*   **Terms of Use:** Datasets may have specific terms of use that outline what you can and cannot do with the data [2]. These terms may include:
    *   Restrictions on commercial use. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-4)
    *   Requirements to include the same acknowledgment in any sub-licenses of the data [2]. [worldbank](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-5)
    *   Disclaimers of warranties and liabilities [2].
*   **DataShop Terms of Use:** For datasets hosted on platforms like DataShop, there may be specific terms of use that apply to the use of those datasets [5].
*   **Open Data Barometer:** The Open Data Barometer (ODB) data is licensed under CC-BY [1]. [landportal](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-6)
*   **World Bank Datasets:** Datasets from the World Bank are provided under a Creative Commons Attribution 4.0 International License (CC BY 4. [worldbank](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-5)0) [2].
*   **Who's On First Dataset:** Crediting Who's On First is recommended, and linking back to the license is required [3]. [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-4)
*   **Pacific Data Hub:** Licenses for datasets on the Pacific Data Hub may vary, with some datasets having no specified license [14, 15]. [pacificdata](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-7)

It's important to check the specific license and terms of use for each dataset before using it to ensure compliance [2, 3].

[github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) The ATS integrates an anomaly scorer with a density-aware sampler to focus on anomaly-rich regions (Source: \\[1, 3, 6]). [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1)\n\nTo use the code, you'll need (Source: \\[2, 7]):\n\n*   Python 3.10 or higher [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)\n*   Pytorch 2.0.1 [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)\n*   CUDA Version 11.7 or higher [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)\n*   Transformers 4.37.2 or higher [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [github](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)\n",

    "Based on the search results, here's a summary of information regarding EventVAD and VADSK for anomaly detection tasks:\n\n**EventVAD:**\n\n*   **Description:** EventVAD is a training-free video anomaly detection framework that combines dynamic graph architectures and multimodal Large Language Models (LLMs) through temporal-event reasoning. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-2) It addresses the limitations of existing training-free methods in localizing fine-grained visual transitions and diverse events within videos. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-2)\n*   **Methodology:**\n    1.  **Event-Aware Dynamic Graph Construction:** Employs dynamic spatiotemporal graph modeling with time-decay constraints to capture event-aware video features. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3)\n    2.  **Graph Attention Networks (GAN) Propagation:** Refines frame representations while preserving temporal consistency using a training-free attention mechanism based on orthogonal feature projection. [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3)\n    3.  **Statistical Boundary Detection:** Performs adaptive noise filtering and uses signal ratio thresholding to detect event boundaries via unsupervised statistical features. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) This reduces the complexity of processing long videos for MLLMs and improves their temporal reasoning through event consistency. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0)\n    4.  **Event-Centric Anomaly Scoring:** Utilizes a hierarchical prompting strategy to guide MLLMs in performing reasoning before determining final decisions.\n*   **Performance:** Achieves state-of-the-art (SOTA) results in training-free settings on the UCF-Crime and XD-Violence datasets, outperforming strong baselines that use 7B or larger MLLMs. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-0) [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-1) [themoonlight](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-3)\n*   **Code:** No code implementations were found in the search results.\n*   **Pre-trained Models/Weights:** EventVAD uses the ViT-B/16 of EVA-CLIP (Sun et al., 2023) and enhances inter-frame features using RAFT optical flow (Teed and Deng, 2020). It inputs the segmented events into an MLLM (Cheng et al., 2024) for scoring. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-2)\n*   **Usage Examples:** Evaluated on the UCF-Crime and XD-Violence datasets.\n\n**VADSK:**\n\n*   **Description:** VADSK is a lightweight pipeline for anomaly classification using keyword weights. It employs a two-stage process: induction followed by deduction. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)\n*   **Methodology:**\n    1.  **Induction:** Descriptions are generated from normal and anomalous frames to identify and assign weights to relevant keywords. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) Randomly sampled normal and anomalous frames are passed through a pre-trained foundational model to output corresponding descriptions of those frames. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-6) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) Next, the normal and anomalous descriptions are passed through a TF-IDF operation, outputting a corresponding TF-IDF matrix of scores. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)\n    2.  **Deduction:** Inference frame descriptions are converted into keyword encodings using induction-derived weights for input into a neural network for anomaly classification. [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4) [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)\n*   **Performance:** Achieved comparable performance on the three benchmarks UCSD Ped2, Shanghai Tech, and CUHK Avenue, with ROC AUC scores of 0.865, 0.745, and 0.742, respectively. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4)\n*   **Code:** No direct link to a GitHub repository was found in the search results.\n*   **Pre-trained Models/Weights:** Uses a pre-trained foundational model to generate captions that differentiate anomaly cases from normal scene behavior. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5)\n*   **Usage Examples:** Evaluated on the UCSD Ped2, Shanghai Tech, and CUHK Avenue datasets. [qeios](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-5) [arxiv](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/6-4)\n\nIt's important to note that both EventVAD and VADSK leverage pre-trained models and/or LLMs to achieve anomaly detection without extensive training data.\n",
    "Based on the search results, here's a summary of anomaly labeling in datasets and the conditions of use:\n\n**Anomaly Labeling in Datasets:**\n\n*   **Types of Anomalies:** Datasets can include various types of anomalies, such as:\n    *   Abnormal events in video sequences, including crashes, fires, and violence [7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-0)\n    *   Anomalous activities detected via webcams [9]. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-1)\n    *   Deviations from the norm in manufacturing, medical imaging, agriculture, retail, and other scenarios [13]. [landing](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-2)\n    *   Contextual anomalies, where events are normal but occur in an unexpected context (e.g., people entering a campus on a weekend) [9].\n    *   Pseudo-contextual anomalies, where existing videos are given an incorrect context label [9]. [thecvf](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-1)\n*   **Labeling Methods:**\n    *   **Video-level labels:** Indicate whether a video is abnormal or normal and the type of anomaly [7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-0)\n    *   **Frame-level labels:** Identify abnormal or normal video frames [7]. [paperswithcode](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-0)\n    *   **Bounding box annotations:** Mark the location of anomalous events within a frame [9].\n    *   **Normal/Abnormal classes:** Datasets may have built-in classes for \"Normal\" and \"Abnormal\" cases [13]. [landing](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/7-2)\n*   **Unlabeled Data:** Some anomaly detection methods work with unlabeled or partially labeled data, identifying patterns without predefined classes [11].
